0375703764|5.0|House of Leaves by Mark Z. Danielewski is a story within a story within a story, but far more complex than that. It may give you nightmares, make you cry, totally un-impress you, or scare the you know what out of you. It will change your life.    A quick summary of the novel: The Navidson family moves into a house. The father, a photojournalist, takes video of their move into a new location. The video quickly turns into a documentary about the house's supernatural qualities. Zampano, the blind recluse, finds the documentary and starts to write a book about it. Truant, the junkie, finds Zampano's book and makes his own notes.     So, there you have the story within a story within a story. Along the way, you'll find that the word \\"House\\" is always written in blue text (if you get the color version of the book), which is the least of the creativity involving typeset. Some pages are written upside down and backwards, while others may contain a single word, or perhaps no words at all. I can guarantee you've never read a novel quite like this one.    I recommend this novel to everyone. Not everyone will like it. In fact, most people won't get through it. Some will think it's brilliant; some will think it's a waste of paper. Regardless of which, it will change their lives and their way of thinking, at least for a little while.    The thing about House of Leaves is that it's not an extraordinary novel at first glance. It appears to be an attempt at avant-garde style. It's a story inside of a story inside of a story that often doesn't make sense. It's filled with unreliable narrators (the drug addict, the blind recluse, and the madly obsessive photo-journalist), endless footnotes, lengthy descriptions and visual tricks. It appears to be an author trying way too hard to do something new.    But it gets under your skin. It scares you when you least expect it. It takes your world and tilts it just a few degrees off-center, just enough to give you an odd disoriented view of the world around you.    After finishing the novel, I wanted to run and hide. Seriously, though, I was relieved when it was done. This was not an easy read. It took me several months, and I had to take breaks from it.    House of Leaves left me feeling disoriented and disconnected. I'm writing this book review one year after starting the novel. Two weeks ago, I had another nightmare about the House. This is probably the most difficult book review I've ever had to write, but I need to write it. This book changed my life, and though I want to share it with others, my review comes with a warning. Odds are, it will change your life, too, and you might not like it.    People equate this novel with the film, The Blair Witch Project, and I've found that the reactions to the novel are similar to those of the film. Either you think it is totally new and it gives you the creeps, or you think it's the dumbest thing you've experienced in your life. For me, House of Leaves is one of the scariest books I've ever read. I've had two nightmares in the year since I started reading it, and I expect to have more.    I found this novel through a message thread on a forum. The title was \\"Books that changed your life.\\" I added it to my ever-growing list of books to read someday, and quickly forgot about it. Then a local bookstore was going out of business, and this happened to be sitting on the shelf of discounted novels. It felt like the book found me when I was least expecting it. And that's really, really scary.

B00386OWUC|5.0|I saw this movie after several notable critics gave it very favorable reviews. On first approach, I can't imagine a film sounding less appealing: a German film, bearing no English audio track, presented in black and white (the film was filmed in color and then had its palette desaturated), concerning the events in a rustic village circa 1914---not exactly Michael Bay material.<br /><br />The film is so anti-establishment, in fact, that some people may recoil from its possible pretentiousness; I include myself in this latter group, having been burned a time or two too often by films buried under their own aspirations of signfiicance.<br /><br />Happily, \\"The White Ribbon\\" bears no such affliction: this is a great, deeply thoughtful movie. There are many adequate discussions here about the film's plot, which I will not belabor, other then to say Michael Haneke's decision to couch his ideas in the framework of a mystery, tinged throughout by a looming sense of dread, was very wise indeed---the viewer is inevitably drawn to the film's narrator/protaganoist as he seeks to uncover the identity of those responsible for the seemingly random acts of violence that have occurred in his village.<br /><br />The less said the better. There are very profound questions being considered here: e.g. how should we balance our personal freeedoms against the communal need for well-being and security---but Haneke is too smart a film maker to offer up an easy fable; there are no simple answers. People are quick to judge the motives of the murderer; the dark nature of a people swept astray by fascism; Haneke suggests the seeds of our worst evils may be sown even in the richest of soils.
1416955070|5.0|City of Bones is set in New York City, but not as we see it--the main character Clary and her friends (who are demon hunters)can see the supernatural world of vampires, werewolves, faeries, demons, warlocks, and other creatures that normal people (mundanes) are blind to.    PLOT  The plot is fast paced for the most part with a love triangle that keeps things interesting. Near the end the reader is suddenly taken on a jerking roller coaster ride of twists. I read a lot and can usually predict twists before they arise, but not the case here. I appreciate when an author can pull off a genuine twist, and Cassandra Clare does it several times.   ***HUGE SPOILER****  One of the huge twists revealed toward the end is that Clary and Jace are siblings, and the villain Valentine is their father. Before knowing this they had been falling for each other. Sound familiar? Think Luke & Leia in Star Wars. Some readers may be annoyed by this twist, and others disappointed like I was. I really liked the romance developing between Jace & Clary and then that twist completely ruined it. I wish they had been love interests instead of siblings.   ****END SPOILER*****      CHARACTERS  I loved the characters. They felt real to me, and it's been a while since I've read a book where I can get attached to them. I even liked the minor characters like Simon, Luke, Isabelle, and Alec. The characters are real, they make mistakes, they argue, they make up, they hate, they love, they cry. Clary was a good heroine--strong but still with weaknesses and flaws. Jace was sexy, sarcastic, tortured, and badass, and will have girls swooning. He could be almost cruel at times but I suppose that's a part of his character. The villain, Valentine, was well-done. It was unnerving to read his scenes, because I couldn't tell whether or not he was lying. I hope to see more character development in the following books.       DIALOGUE  The dialogue was good and enjoyable, with lots of sarcastic, witty, humorous banter between characters. But there was one thing that bothered me--throughout the book the characters used huge words in their sarcastic banter that not even I know the meaning of and I'm a college student. And the characters are what, 15? 16? For example, Clary says, \\"When the self-congratulatory part of the evening is over, maybe we could get back to saving my best friend from being exsanguinated to death?\\" In some instances it was okay, but in this example a simpler word would have done better. It just made it feel unrealistic at times, because teenagers don't talk like that. (Not to say teenagers can't use big words, but some of the words used were a bit of a stretch)       WRITING  City of Bones is very well-written. However, a few times the descriptions didn't make sense or the prose made me wince. For example, at one point Clary is eating an apple and it's described as tasting, \\"green and cool.\\" This actually made me cringe. How can you taste a color? This could easily have been remedied with some sharper editing.      Despite the few nitpicks I have with it, I highly recommend City of Bones. It's an entertaining read and you won't want to put it down! If you're not certain check out the first from the library, and I guraentee more than likely you'll be buying the second before you've even finished the first, just like I did.

B003PIUC02|5.0|Alright, after reading a handful of one-star reviews, I get it...I really do.    In fact, even though I should've known better, initially even *I* had a negative reaction the first two episodes. The acting/dialog was suspect; the actors were utterly generic/unknown; the \\"battle\\" scenes were completely unrealistic, over-the-top cgi-fests; and I didn't really care about any of the characters. Especially \\"Spartacus\\"!    Like I said. I get it.    Having said that, I stuck with it because I realized two VERY important factors where hampering my ability to enjoy the series:    First and most importantly, was the fact that I allowed my expectations to be set by the initial main-stream reviews. I am greatly into \\"period\\" pieces; the less civilized the period, the better I like it, because, and I make no apologies, in addition to loving the stilted language and protocol of classed societies, I am a blood and guts kinda guy. So when the reviewers went on about the blood and violence, quite naturally, I expected realistic depictions of brutality and violence, ala \\"Gladiator\\". I also expected expensive sets and costumes, and great acting by all involved. In other words, I was expecting a 150+ million dollar, big screen production instead of an original CABLE series...And not even an HBO series at that.    So, after adjusting my expectations, and judging the series on the basis of its own merits, I realized that A. The acting improved, and characters become MUCH more interesting. B. The cgi-ifying of the violence, and it's stylized outlandishness was intentional, making it almost \\"operatic\\", and easier to stomach. The bloodletting, was literally a work of art in motion, like ballet. Yes, it borrowed from the movie 300, but I believe it took it to the next level. The sets remained low budget, but to ME, this series wasn't about the sets, or really, with the exception of maybe three or four battle scenes, not even the arena. Which brings me to the second realization.    Like a number of series deemed as low-budget and/or cheesy by those, not in the know, the beauty and magnificence of this series lies in the characters and storyline. A perfect comparison for me personally, would be the \\"Buffy the Vampire Slayer\\", and \\"Angel\\" series. My first take on both of those series (especially Buffy) was cheesy, and b-level at best. In fact, you can even add \\"Firefly\\" to the list. But today, ALL three of them rate as some of my ALL TIME favorite series, which I have re-watched in their entirety, multiple times since they went off the air. The same is true for \\"Spartacus\\". And no, these aren't cases of getting beat over the head with something you hate, until you love it. It was about giving the series enough time to understand the over-arching storyline, and to decide whether or not the characters were worth spending time with every week.    In the case of Spartacus, the characters are so vivid, that there was not a single main character that I felt apathetic towards. I had strong feelings one way or another for each of them. So much so, that I am not ashamed to admit that I actually cried when one died. After several viewings, tears STILL run down my cheeks when the character meets their end. In fact, I tear up, just thinking about it, as I write this review. And trust me, I'm a 47-year old tough guy...Well, at least I USED to be. lol.    And isn't THAT what great media, be it a painting, book, movie, or television is supposed to do?    Move us?    Come for the action, blood, and/or hot women/beefcake, but you'll stay for the characters, relationships, and the storyline.
